What is the purpose of brining?::Brining adds moisture and flavor to meat by soaking it in a saltwater solution.
How do I prevent avocado from browning?::Brush it with lemon or lime juice and store it in an airtight container.
What is tempering chocolate?::Tempering stabilizes chocolate by melting and cooling it to achieve a glossy finish and proper snap.
How do I know when fish is cooked?::Fish is done when it flakes easily with a fork and appears opaque throughout.
What is the difference between simmering and boiling?::Simmering involves cooking at a lower temperature with small bubbles, while boiling has larger, rolling bubbles.
How do I prevent rice from sticking?::Rinse the rice before cooking and use the correct water-to-rice ratio.
What is al dente?::Al dente refers to pasta or rice cooked until firm to the bite, not mushy.
What is the best way to chop onions without crying?::Chill the onion, use a sharp knife, and cut near a fan or under running water.
How do I prevent pancakes from sticking to the pan?::Use a non-stick pan or griddle and lightly grease it with butter or oil before cooking.
What is folding in baking?::Folding gently incorporates ingredients to maintain airiness, such as in whipped cream or egg whites.
How do I make homemade whipped cream?::Beat cold heavy cream with sugar and vanilla until soft peaks form.
What is the purpose of resting dough?::Resting dough relaxes gluten and allows flavors to develop.
What is the difference between sautéing and frying?::Sautéing uses less oil and high heat for quick cooking, while frying involves submerging food in hot oil.
How do I prevent a pie crust from getting soggy?::Blind bake the crust or brush it with egg wash before adding the filling.
What is the best way to peel a tomato?::Blanch it in boiling water for a few seconds, then transfer it to ice water to loosen the skin.
What is zesting?::Zesting is removing the outer, colorful layer of citrus peel for flavor.
How do I properly rest bread after baking?::Let it cool on a wire rack to prevent sogginess from trapped steam.
What is a slurry?::A slurry is a mixture of cornstarch and water used to thicken soups or sauces.
What is the purpose of an ice bath in cooking?::An ice bath rapidly cools food to stop the cooking process and preserve texture.
How do I prevent a cheesecake from cracking?::Use a water bath and avoid overmixing the batter.
What is the best way to toast nuts?::Toast them in a dry pan or oven to bring out their natural oils and enhance flavor.
What is julienning?::Julienning is cutting food into thin, matchstick-like strips.
What is the difference between clarified butter and regular butter?::Clarified butter has milk solids removed, making it suitable for high-heat cooking.
What is the best way to clean cast iron?::Use hot water and a scrub brush; avoid soap and dry thoroughly to prevent rust.
How do I prevent mashed potatoes from becoming gummy?::Avoid over-mixing and use warm milk or butter for mashing.
What is glazing in cooking?::Glazing adds a shiny coating to food, often using a mixture of sugar, water, or sauce.
What is the best way to cook a steak?::Sear on high heat, finish in the oven, and rest before slicing.
How do I measure sticky ingredients like honey?::Coat the measuring spoon or cup with oil to help the honey slide out easily.
What is a bain-marie?::A bain-marie is a water bath used to gently heat food or keep it warm.
What is the difference between braising and stewing?::Braising uses less liquid and larger cuts of meat, while stewing uses more liquid and smaller pieces.
What is chiffonade?::Chiffonade is a slicing technique for leafy greens or herbs into thin ribbons.
How do I prevent cookies from spreading too much?::Chill the dough before baking and use a parchment-lined baking sheet.
What is the purpose of sifting flour?::Sifting aerates the flour and removes lumps for lighter baked goods.
What is emulsifying in cooking?::Emulsifying combines two liquids, like oil and vinegar, into a stable mixture.
How do I make homemade stock?::Simmer bones, vegetables, and herbs in water for several hours, then strain.
What is blind baking?::Blind baking pre-cooks a pie crust before adding the filling.
How do I fix a broken sauce?::Whisk in a little warm water or butter to re-emulsify it.
What is the difference between creaming and mixing?::Creaming involves beating butter and sugar until light, while mixing combines ingredients uniformly.
What is the best way to slice bread?::Use a serrated knife for clean, even slices.
How do I make homemade pasta?::Mix flour and eggs to form a dough, roll it out, and cut into desired shapes.
What is sweating in cooking?::Sweating involves gently cooking vegetables in a little oil or butter to soften without browning.
What is parboiling?::Parboiling partially cooks food in boiling water before finishing it with another method.
How do I prevent chocolate chips from sinking in a cake?::Toss them in flour before adding them to the batter.
What is the difference between a vinaigrette and a dressing?::A vinaigrette is oil and vinegar-based, while dressing can include creamy or other types of bases.
How do I store leftover soup?::Cool it completely and store in an airtight container in the fridge or freezer.
What is spatchcocking?::Spatchcocking is removing a chicken’s backbone so it can lay flat for even cooking.
What is the best way to cut raw meat?::Use a sharp knife and slice against the grain for tenderness.
What is the difference between fresh and dried herbs?::Fresh herbs are milder and often added at the end of cooking, while dried herbs have concentrated flavor and are used earlier.
How do I make homemade breadcrumbs?::Pulse stale bread in a food processor until crumbly.
What is resting in cooking?::Resting allows food, especially meat, to retain its juices and settle before serving.
What is the purpose of acid in cooking?::Acid enhances flavor, tenderizes proteins, and balances sweetness or richness.
How do I prevent overcooking shrimp?::Cook until they turn pink and opaque, which only takes a few minutes.
What is cross-contamination?::Cross-contamination is the transfer of harmful bacteria from one food or surface to another.
What is the best way to grill vegetables?::Toss them in oil and seasoning, and grill until tender and slightly charred.
What is dredging?::Dredging involves coating food in flour or breadcrumbs before cooking.
How do I make homemade caramel?::Heat sugar over medium heat until melted and golden brown, then add butter and cream.
What is compound butter?::Compound butter is softened butter mixed with herbs, spices, or other flavorings.
What is the best way to cook eggs sunny-side up?::Cook on low heat with a lid to set the whites while keeping the yolk runny.
How do I prevent pie crust from shrinking?::Chill the dough and avoid stretching it when rolling out.
What is poaching?::Poaching involves cooking food gently in simmering liquid, like water or broth.
What is a reduction in cooking?::A reduction concentrates flavors by simmering liquids until thickened.
How do I temper eggs?::Slowly whisk hot liquid into beaten eggs to prevent curdling.
What is the best way to season cast iron?::Coat it with oil and bake upside down in a hot oven to build a non-stick surface.
What is the purpose of an egg wash?::An egg wash adds color and shine to baked goods or seals edges.
How do I make flaky biscuits?::Use cold butter and handle the dough minimally to avoid overworking it.
What is the best way to roast garlic?::Slice the top off a garlic bulb, drizzle with oil, wrap in foil, and roast until soft.
How do I prevent cake layers from doming?::Use bake-even strips or lower the oven temperature slightly.
What is a bouquet garni?::A bouquet garni is a bundle of herbs tied together or placed in a sachet for easy removal after cooking.
How do I prevent custard from curdling?::Cook it slowly over low heat and stir constantly.
What is the purpose of salt in baking?::Salt enhances flavor and controls yeast activity in dough.
How do I make perfect French fries?::Soak cut potatoes in water to remove starch, then fry twice for crispiness.
What is a water bath in baking?::A water bath surrounds a baking dish with hot water for even, gentle cooking.
What is machine learning?::Machine learning is a branch of AI that enables systems to learn and improve from data without explicit programming.
What is cybersecurity?::Cybersecurity involves protecting computers, networks, and data from unauthorized access or attacks.
What is a LAN (Local Area Network)?::A LAN is a network that connects computers within a small geographical area, such as an office or home.
What is a WAN (Wide Area Network)?::A WAN connects computers across large geographical areas, often using telecommunication lines.
What is the Internet?::The Internet is a global network of interconnected computers that share information using standardized communication protocols.
What is an IP address?::An IP address is a unique identifier assigned to devices on a network to enable communication.
What is a URL?::A URL (Uniform Resource Locator) is the address used to access resources on the Internet, such as websites.
What is an operating system?::An operating system is system software that manages hardware and software resources and provides common services for applications.
What is multitasking in computing?::Multitasking refers to the ability of an operating system to run multiple tasks or processes simultaneously.
What is a programming language?::A programming language is a formal language used to write instructions that a computer can execute.
What is object-oriented programming?::Object-oriented programming is a paradigm based on the concept of objects, which contain data and methods to manipulate that data.
What is a flowchart?::A flowchart is a graphical representation of a process or algorithm using symbols to depict steps and their sequence.
What is an array?::An array is a data structure that stores a collection of items, typically of the same data type, in a contiguous memory location.
What is recursion?::Recursion is a programming technique where a function calls itself to solve smaller instances of a problem.
What is a motherboard?::The motherboard is the main circuit board of a computer that connects all components, including the CPU, RAM, and storage.
What is RAM?::RAM (Random Access Memory) is a type of volatile memory used to store data temporarily for active processes.
What is ROM?::ROM (Read-Only Memory) is non-volatile memory used to store firmware or permanent instructions for a computer.
What is a hard drive?::A hard drive is a storage device used to store and retrieve digital information, including the operating system and applications.
What is a solid-state drive (SSD)?::An SSD is a high-speed storage device that uses flash memory to store data, offering faster performance than traditional hard drives.
What is virtualization?::Virtualization is the process of creating a virtual version of something, such as hardware, storage, or an operating system.
What is a firewall?::A firewall is a security system that monitors and controls incoming and outgoing network traffic based on predetermined rules.
What is encryption?::Encryption is the process of converting data into a coded format to prevent unauthorized access.
What is the difference between TCP and UDP?::TCP is a connection-oriented protocol ensuring data delivery, while UDP is connectionless and faster but less reliable.
What is HTTP?::HTTP (HyperText Transfer Protocol) is the protocol used for transmitting web pages over the Internet.
What is HTTPS?::HTTPS (HyperText Transfer Protocol Secure) is a secure version of HTTP that encrypts data using SSL/TLS.
What is a database management system (DBMS)?::A DBMS is software that enables the creation, management, and querying of databases.
What is a primary key in a database?::A primary key is a unique identifier for each record in a database table.
What is SQL?::SQL (Structured Query Language) is a language used to interact with and manage data in a relational database.
What is the difference between a virus and a worm?::A virus attaches to files and requires user action to spread, while a worm replicates and spreads independently.
What is phishing?::Phishing is a cyberattack where attackers trick users into providing sensitive information, often via deceptive emails or websites.
What is data mining?::Data mining is the process of discovering patterns and insights from large datasets using statistical and computational methods.
What is big data?::Big data refers to extremely large datasets that require advanced tools and techniques to process and analyze.
What is a peer-to-peer network?::In a peer-to-peer network, devices share resources directly without requiring a central server.
What is cloud storage?::Cloud storage is a service that allows users to store data on remote servers accessed via the Internet.
What is a digital signature?::A digital signature is a cryptographic method used to verify the authenticity and integrity of digital documents.
What is a MAC address?::A MAC (Media Access Control) address is a unique identifier assigned to a network interface card for communication within a network.
What is the function of a router?::A router directs data packets between networks, enabling communication between devices on different networks.
What is a proxy server?::A proxy server acts as an intermediary between a client and the Internet, improving privacy and security.
What is a virtual private network (VPN)?::A VPN creates a secure, encrypted connection over a less secure network, such as the Internet.
What is artificial neural network (ANN)?::ANN is a computing system inspired by the human brain, used in machine learning to recognize patterns and solve problems.
What is a compiler?::A compiler translates high-level source code into machine code that a computer can execute.
What is a query?::A query is a request for information from a database, often written in SQL.
What is multitier architecture?::Multitier architecture separates an application into layers, such as presentation, business logic, and data storage, for scalability and maintainability.
What is normalization in databases?::Normalization is the process of organizing data to reduce redundancy and improve data integrity.
What is an API?::An API (Application Programming Interface) is a set of rules and tools for building software and allowing applications to communicate.
What is an IDE?::An IDE (Integrated Development Environment) is software that provides tools for writing, debugging, and testing code.
What is data abstraction?::Data abstraction hides the complexities of data, exposing only essential features to users or applications.
What is a kernel?::The kernel is the core of an operating system, managing system resources and communication between hardware and software.
What is a cache memory?::Cache memory is a small, high-speed storage area located close to the CPU, used to store frequently accessed data and instructions.
What is IPv6?::IPv6 is the latest version of the Internet Protocol, designed to provide a larger address space and improved security compared to IPv4.
What is a hash function?::A hash function is a mathematical function that converts input data into a fixed-size string, often used in data indexing and encryption.
What is the difference between a stack and a queue?::A stack follows LIFO (Last In, First Out) order, while a queue follows FIFO (First In, First Out) order.
What is a distributed system?::A distributed system is a network of independent computers that work together to appear as a single system to users.
What is virtualization in cloud computing?::Virtualization in cloud computing creates virtual instances of servers, storage, or networks to optimize resource use.
What is metadata?::Metadata is data that describes other data, providing information like format, structure, or purpose.
What is packet switching?::Packet switching is a method of data transmission where data is broken into packets and sent independently across the network.
What is an assembler?::An assembler is a tool that translates assembly language into machine code for execution by the CPU.
What is the difference between primary and secondary memory?::Primary memory (like RAM) is volatile and fast, while secondary memory (like hard drives) is non-volatile and used for long-term storage.
What is a thread in computing?::A thread is a lightweight process that shares resources with other threads within the same application.
What is a semaphore?::A semaphore is a synchronization tool used to manage access to shared resources in concurrent programming.
What is a deadlock?::A deadlock occurs when two or more processes are unable to proceed because each is waiting for the other to release a resource.
What is a hash table?::A hash table is a data structure that maps keys to values using a hash function for fast lookups.
What is a linked list?::A linked list is a linear data structure where each element (node) points to the next, allowing dynamic memory allocation.
What is a binary search tree?::A binary search tree is a hierarchical data structure where each node has up to two children, and nodes are arranged by value.
What is cloud deployment?::Cloud deployment refers to hosting applications and services in the cloud, including public, private, or hybrid models.
What is a protocol?::A protocol is a set of rules governing communication between devices in a network.
What is a session in web development?::A session is a temporary interaction between a user and a web application, often tracked using cookies or session IDs.
What is middleware?::Middleware is software that acts as a bridge between applications, enabling them to communicate and work together.
What is a sandbox?::A sandbox is an isolated testing environment where software can run securely without affecting the system.
What is a virtual machine?::A virtual machine is a software-based emulation of a physical computer, running an operating system and applications.
What is a buffer?::A buffer is a temporary storage area for data being transferred between devices or processes.
What is a process?::A process is an instance of a program in execution, consisting of code, data, and system resources.
What is a daemon?::A daemon is a background process that performs specific tasks or services without direct user interaction.
What is a compiler optimization?::Compiler optimization improves code efficiency and performance during the compilation process without changing functionality.
What is an inode?::An inode is a data structure used in file systems to store information about a file, such as its size, location, and permissions.
What is a filesystem?::A filesystem is a method for organizing and storing data on storage devices, allowing users to retrieve and manage files.
What is a queue in networking?::A queue in networking is a data structure used to manage packets waiting for processing or transmission.
What is a MAC (Message Authentication Code)?::A MAC ensures data integrity and authenticity by generating a cryptographic checksum based on the message and a secret key.
What is DNS?::DNS (Domain Name System) translates human-readable domain names into IP addresses, enabling users to access websites.
What is latency in networking?::Latency is the delay between a user's action and a network's response, typically measured in milliseconds.
What is the difference between static and dynamic IP addresses?::A static IP address is fixed, while a dynamic IP address changes periodically, assigned by a DHCP server.
What is a Trojan horse in cybersecurity?::A Trojan horse is malicious software disguised as legitimate software to trick users into installing it.
What is a man-in-the-middle attack?::A man-in-the-middle attack occurs when an attacker intercepts communication between two parties to steal data or inject malicious content.
What is digital forensics?::Digital forensics is the practice of recovering, analyzing, and presenting digital evidence in legal or investigative scenarios.
What is a logic gate?::A logic gate is a basic building block of digital circuits that performs a logical operation (e.g., AND, OR, NOT).
What is Boolean algebra?::Boolean algebra is a branch of algebra dealing with true or false values, used in digital logic design.
What is a compiler error?::A compiler error is a syntax or semantic issue in code that prevents successful compilation.
What is an interrupt?::An interrupt is a signal to the processor indicating an event that needs immediate attention, pausing the current process.
What is paging in memory management?::Paging is a memory management technique that divides memory into fixed-size pages to reduce fragmentation.
What is a relational database?::A relational database stores data in tables with relationships between them, using keys to maintain data integrity.
What is data redundancy?::Data redundancy occurs when the same data is stored in multiple places, leading to inefficiency and potential inconsistencies.
What is a graph in computer science?::A graph is a data structure consisting of nodes (vertices) connected by edges, used to model relationships.
What is a spanning tree?::A spanning tree is a subgraph of a connected graph that includes all the vertices with the minimum number of edges.
What is normalization in databases?::Normalization is the process of organizing data to eliminate redundancy and ensure dependencies are logical.
What is a tuple in databases?::A tuple is a single row or record in a database table, representing a set of related data.
What is a primary key?::A primary key is a unique identifier for a row in a database table.
What is a foreign key?::A foreign key is a field in a database table that establishes a relationship with a primary key in another table.
What is NoSQL?::NoSQL is a type of database that provides flexible schemas and is optimized for unstructured data, unlike traditional relational databases.
What is an index in a database?::An index is a data structure that improves the speed of data retrieval in a database at the cost of additional storage.
What is SQL injection?::SQL injection is a security vulnerability that allows attackers to manipulate queries by injecting malicious SQL code.
What is two-factor authentication (2FA)?::2FA is a security method requiring two verification steps, such as a password and a one-time code, to enhance protection.
What is a software development life cycle (SDLC)?::The SDLC is a structured process for planning, developing, testing, and deploying software.
What is version control?::Version control is a system for tracking changes to files or code, enabling collaboration and history tracking.
What is an API endpoint?::An API endpoint is a specific URL where a client sends requests to access a particular resource or service.
What is polymorphism in OOP?::Polymorphism allows objects to be treated as instances of their parent class while executing their unique behaviors.
What is encapsulation in OOP?::Encapsulation is the practice of bundling data and methods that operate on the data within a single unit, such as a class.
What is inheritance in OOP?::Inheritance is an OOP concept where a class derives properties and methods from another class, promoting code reuse.
What is a constructor in programming?::A constructor is a special method in a class that initializes objects when they are created.
What is an interface in programming?::An interface is a blueprint that defines a set of methods that a class must implement.
What is a module in programming?::A module is a file containing code (functions, classes) that can be reused in other programs.
What is a library in programming?::A library is a collection of pre-written code that developers can use to optimize the development process.
What is multithreading?::Multithreading is a programming concept where multiple threads run concurrently, improving performance in multitasking.
What is a dynamic data structure?::A dynamic data structure can change in size during runtime, such as linked lists or dynamic arrays.
What is a stack overflow?::A stack overflow occurs when a program exceeds the maximum size of the call stack, often due to excessive recursion.
What is a garbage collector?::A garbage collector is a system process that automatically frees memory occupied by objects no longer in use.
What is a bit?::A bit is the smallest unit of data in computing, representing a binary value of 0 or 1.
What is a byte?::A byte consists of 8 bits and is commonly used as a unit of digital storage or data transfer.
What is ASCII?::ASCII (American Standard Code for Information Interchange) is a character encoding standard for text in computers.
What is Unicode?::Unicode is a universal character encoding standard that supports text representation for most writing systems.
What is a checksum?::A checksum is a value calculated from a data set to verify its integrity during storage or transmission.
What is an embedded system?::An embedded system is a computer system designed to perform dedicated functions within a larger system.
What is pipelining in processors?::Pipelining is a technique where multiple instruction stages are processed simultaneously to increase CPU performance.
What is the Von Neumann architecture?::Von Neumann architecture is a computer design model where the program and data share the same memory and communication pathways.
What is clock speed in processors?::Clock speed measures how many cycles a CPU executes per second, typically expressed in gigahertz (GHz).
What is an instruction set?::An instruction set is a collection of commands a CPU can execute to perform specific tasks.
What is a floating-point number?::A floating-point number represents real numbers, allowing for fractional values and very large or small numbers.
What is a relational operator?::A relational operator compares two values, returning a boolean result (e.g., ==, !=, >, <).
What is a logical operator?::A logical operator combines boolean expressions (e.g., AND, OR, NOT) to return a boolean value.
What is a loop in programming?::A loop is a control structure that repeats a block of code as long as a specified condition is true.
What is an infinite loop?::An infinite loop is a loop that never terminates because its condition always evaluates to true.
What is exception handling?::Exception handling manages errors during program execution, ensuring the program continues running or exits gracefully.
What is the difference between a stack and a heap?::The stack is used for static memory allocation, while the heap is used for dynamic memory allocation.
What is a regular expression?::A regular expression is a pattern used to match, search, and manipulate text.
What is a token in programming?::A token is a small unit of a program, such as a keyword, operator, or identifier.
What is a debugger?::A debugger is a tool that helps developers test and debug code by identifying and fixing errors.
What is a breakpoint in debugging?::A breakpoint is a marker set in code to pause execution, allowing developers to examine the program's state.
What is API rate limiting?::API rate limiting restricts the number of requests a client can make to an API within a specified time frame.
What is a microservice?::A microservice is a small, independent service that performs a specific function within a larger application.
What is a container in software?::A container is a lightweight, portable software package that includes an application and its dependencies.
What is a kernel panic?::A kernel panic is a system error that occurs when the operating system cannot recover from a critical issue.
What is a bootloader?::A bootloader is a program that loads an operating system into memory and initializes the system at startup.
What is a system call?::A system call is a request made by a program to the operating system for a specific service, such as file access.
What is a process scheduler?::A process scheduler manages the execution of processes by allocating CPU time and resources.
What is a device driver?::A device driver is software that allows the operating system to interact with hardware devices.
What is RAID?::RAID (Redundant Array of Independent Disks) is a storage technology that combines multiple drives to improve performance or reliability.
What is NAT in networking?::NAT (Network Address Translation) translates private IP addresses to a public IP address for devices in a local network to access the Internet.
What is a subnet mask?::A subnet mask defines the range of IP addresses in a network, distinguishing between the network and host portions.
What is an autonomous system?::An autonomous system is a collection of IP networks under the control of a single organization with a unified routing policy.
What is SSL/TLS?::SSL (Secure Sockets Layer) and TLS (Transport Layer Security) are cryptographic protocols that secure communication over the Internet.
What is bandwidth in networking?::Bandwidth is the maximum amount of data that can be transmitted over a network in a given time, measured in bits per second (bps).
What is a digital certificate?::A digital certificate is an electronic document that proves the ownership of a public key, issued by a certificate authority.
What is a routing table?::A routing table stores information about routes to different network destinations for efficient packet delivery.
What is IPv4?::IPv4 (Internet Protocol version 4) is the fourth version of the Internet Protocol, using a 32-bit address format.
What is traceroute?::Traceroute is a network diagnostic tool that traces the path packets take to reach a destination.
What is a botnet?::A botnet is a network of infected devices controlled by a hacker, often used for malicious activities like DDoS attacks.
What is two's complement?::Two's complement is a binary representation for signed integers, enabling addition and subtraction of positive and negative numbers.
What is instruction pipelining?::Instruction pipelining breaks down CPU instructions into smaller steps that are executed simultaneously for better performance.
What is a cache miss?::A cache miss occurs when the CPU cannot find the requested data in the cache and must fetch it from slower memory.
What is latency in cloud computing?::Latency in cloud computing refers to the delay between a user request and the cloud service’s response.
What is edge computing?::Edge computing processes data closer to the source of generation, reducing latency and bandwidth usage.
What is a hypervisor?::A hypervisor is software that creates and manages virtual machines by allocating physical resources.
What is a load balancer?::A load balancer distributes incoming network traffic across multiple servers to ensure reliability and performance.
What is DHCP?::DHCP (Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol) is a protocol that automatically assigns IP addresses to devices on a network.
What is ARP?::ARP (Address Resolution Protocol) translates IP addresses into MAC addresses for communication within a local network.
What is packet sniffing?::Packet sniffing is the process of capturing and analyzing network traffic to monitor or troubleshoot networks.
What is SSH?::SSH (Secure Shell) is a protocol that provides secure remote login and command execution over an unsecured network.
What is FTP?::FTP (File Transfer Protocol) is a standard protocol used to transfer files between a client and server over a network.
What is a hash collision?::A hash collision occurs when two different inputs produce the same hash value, potentially compromising data integrity.
What is a bloom filter?::A bloom filter is a probabilistic data structure used to test whether an element is a member of a set, with possible false positives.
What is a CDN?::A CDN (Content Delivery Network) is a system of distributed servers that delivers web content to users based on their geographic location.
What is big-endian?::Big-endian is a data format where the most significant byte is stored at the smallest memory address.
What is little-endian?::Little-endian is a data format where the least significant byte is stored at the smallest memory address.
What is a digital twin?::A digital twin is a virtual model of a physical object or system, used for monitoring, simulation, and analysis.
What is middleware in distributed systems?::Middleware is software that provides common services and communication capabilities for distributed applications.
What is fault tolerance?::Fault tolerance is the ability of a system to continue functioning in the event of hardware or software failure.
What is scalability in computing?::Scalability is the ability of a system to handle increasing workloads by adding resources such as servers or storage.
What is a data warehouse?::A data warehouse is a central repository for storing and analyzing large volumes of structured and historical data.
What is OLTP?::OLTP (Online Transaction Processing) refers to systems optimized for managing transaction-oriented applications.
What is OLAP?::OLAP (Online Analytical Processing) refers to systems optimized for querying and analyzing data in a multidimensional database.
What is a neural network?::A neural network is a machine learning model inspired by the human brain, consisting of layers of interconnected nodes.
What is backpropagation?::Backpropagation is an algorithm used in training neural networks by adjusting weights based on errors.
What is supervised learning?::Supervised learning is a type of machine learning where a model is trained on labeled data to make predictions.
What is unsupervised learning?::Unsupervised learning is a type of machine learning where a model identifies patterns and structures in unlabeled data.
What is reinforcement learning?::Reinforcement learning is a type of machine learning where an agent learns to make decisions by maximizing rewards.
What is a feature in machine learning?::A feature is an individual measurable property or characteristic used as input for a machine learning model.
What is overfitting?::Overfitting occurs when a machine learning model performs well on training data but poorly on unseen data.
What is underfitting?::Underfitting occurs when a machine learning model fails to capture the underlying patterns in the data.
What is a decision tree?::A decision tree is a machine learning algorithm that splits data into branches based on conditions to make predictions.
What is a random forest?::A random forest is an ensemble learning method that uses multiple decision trees to improve predictive accuracy.
What is clustering?::Clustering is a technique in unsupervised learning that groups similar data points into clusters based on features.
What is a convolutional neural network (CNN)?::A CNN is a type of neural network designed for processing structured data like images.
What is a recurrent neural network (RNN)?::An RNN is a type of neural network that processes sequential data by retaining information from previous steps.
What is a GAN?::A GAN (Generative Adversarial Network) is a machine learning model that generates new data by pitting two networks against each other.
What is a hyperparameter in machine learning?::A hyperparameter is a parameter set before training a model, affecting its structure or learning process.
What is a confusion matrix?::A confusion matrix is a table used to evaluate the performance of a classification algorithm, showing true and false positives and negatives.
What is IoT?::IoT (Internet of Things) refers to a network of interconnected devices that collect and exchange data using sensors and software.
What is a smart device?::A smart device is an IoT-enabled gadget that can connect to a network and perform tasks autonomously or interactively.
What is data integrity?::Data integrity ensures the accuracy and consistency of data throughout its lifecycle.
What is a blockchain?::A blockchain is a decentralized ledger of transactions that is secure and immutable.
What is a smart contract?::A smart contract is self-executing code on a blockchain that enforces and automates agreement terms.
What is a decentralized application (dApp)?::A dApp is an application that runs on a decentralized network, like a blockchain, rather than a centralized server.
What is cryptocurrency mining?::Cryptocurrency mining involves verifying blockchain transactions and adding them to the ledger while earning rewards.

What is proof of stake?::Proof of stake is a consensus mechanism where participants validate transactions based on the number of coins they hold.
What is a digital ledger?::A digital ledger is an electronic record system for tracking and recording transactions or assets.

What is REST?::REST (Representational State Transfer) is an architectural style for designing networked applications using stateless communication.

What is continuous delivery?::Continuous delivery automates the deployment of code changes to staging or production environments after testing.
What is a flowchart in computer science?::A flowchart is a diagram that represents a process or algorithm using standard symbols like rectangles, diamonds, and arrows.

What is Boolean logic?::Boolean logic is a branch of algebra dealing with true or false values, used in decision-making and logical operations.
What is a truth table?::A truth table is a table used to display the output of a Boolean expression for all possible input combinations.
What is a NOT gate?::A NOT gate is a logic gate that inverts its input; it outputs 1 if the input is 0, and vice versa.
What is an AND gate?::An AND gate is a logic gate that outputs 1 only if all its inputs are 1.
What is an OR gate?::An OR gate is a logic gate that outputs 1 if any of its inputs is 1.
What is a NAND gate?::A NAND gate is a combination of AND and NOT gates; it outputs 0 only if all its inputs are 1.
What is a NOR gate?::A NOR gate is a combination of OR and NOT gates; it outputs 1 only if all its inputs are 0.
What is ASCII used for?::ASCII is a character encoding standard that represents text in computers using numerical codes.
What is a variable in programming?::A variable is a named storage location in memory that holds a value, which can be changed during program execution.
What is a constant in programming?::A constant is a value in programming that does not change during the execution of a program.
What is an identifier in programming?::An identifier is the name used to identify variables, constants, functions, or other elements in a program.
What is a data type?::A data type specifies the type of data a variable can store, such as integers, floating-point numbers, or characters.
What is a conditional statement?::A conditional statement is a control structure that executes a block of code based on a specified condition, such as `if` or `else`.
What is a loop?::A loop is a programming construct that repeats a block of code while a condition is true, such as `for`, `while`, or `do-while`.
What is a function in programming?::A function is a reusable block of code designed to perform a specific task when called.
What is an array in programming?::An array is a data structure that stores a fixed-size sequence of elements of the same data type.
What is a two-dimensional array?::A two-dimensional array is an array of arrays, used to represent data in rows and columns, like a matrix.
What is a string?::A string is a sequence of characters treated as a single data element in programming.
What is a file in computing?::A file is a named collection of data stored on a storage device.

What is a logical error?::A logical error is a mistake in the program's logic that produces incorrect results despite running without crashing.

What is Java?::Java is a high-level, object-oriented programming language known for its portability, robustness, and platform independence.

What is bytecode in Java?::Bytecode is the intermediate representation of Java code, which the JVM executes.
What is the Java Development Kit (JDK)?::The JDK is a software package that provides tools like a compiler, debugger, and libraries needed to develop Java programs.
What is the Java Runtime Environment (JRE)?::The JRE is the part of the JDK that provides the libraries and JVM required to run Java applications.
What is an object in Java?::An object is an instance of a class that contains state (fields) and behavior (methods).
What is a class in Java?::A class is a blueprint for creating objects, defining their properties and methods.
What is a method in Java?::A method is a block of code that performs a specific task and is associated with an object or class.
What is a constructor in Java?::A constructor is a special method used to initialize objects when they are created.
What is inheritance in Java?::Inheritance is a mechanism where one class can derive properties and methods from another class.
What is polymorphism in Java?::Polymorphism in Java allows methods to perform different tasks based on the object that calls them.
What is encapsulation in Java?::Encapsulation is the bundling of data (fields) and methods that operate on that data within a single class, and restricting access using access modifiers.
What is abstraction in Java?::Abstraction in Java hides implementation details and only exposes essential features of an object through interfaces or abstract classes.
What is an interface in Java?::An interface in Java is a collection of abstract methods that a class can implement to define specific behaviors.
What is an abstract class in Java?::An abstract class is a class that cannot be instantiated and may contain abstract methods that must be implemented by subclasses.
What are access modifiers in Java?::Access modifiers define the visibility of classes, methods, and fields; common modifiers are `public`, `private`, `protected`, and default.
What is the `main` method in Java?::The `main` method is the entry point of a Java program, defined as `public static void main(String[] args)`.
What is the difference between `static` and instance methods in Java?::Static methods belong to the class and can be called without an object, while instance methods require an object of the class to be called.
What is the `this` keyword in Java?::The `this` keyword refers to the current object and is used to access its members or call its methods.
What is the `super` keyword in Java?::The `super` keyword is used to call a parent class's constructor or methods.
What is method overloading in Java?::Method overloading allows multiple methods in a class to have the same name but different parameter lists.
What is method overriding in Java?::Method overriding allows a subclass to provide a specific implementation for a method defined in its parent class.
What is a package in Java?::A package is a namespace that organizes classes and interfaces, making code easier to manage and avoid name conflicts.
What is the `import` keyword in Java?::The `import` keyword is used to include a package or specific classes from a package in a Java program.
What are wrapper classes in Java?::Wrapper classes provide object representations of primitive data types, such as `Integer` for `int` and `Double` for `double`.
What is autoboxing in Java?::Autoboxing is the automatic conversion of primitive types to their corresponding wrapper class objects.
What is unboxing in Java?::Unboxing is the automatic conversion of wrapper class objects back to their corresponding primitive types.
What is an exception in Java?::An exception is an event that disrupts the normal flow of a program and can be handled using `try-catch` blocks.
What is a checked exception in Java?::Checked exceptions are exceptions that must be declared in the `throws` clause or handled using `try-catch`, such as `IOException`.
What is an unchecked exception in Java?::Unchecked exceptions are exceptions that do not need to be declared or handled, such as `ArithmeticException`.
What is a try-catch block in Java?::A try-catch block is used to handle exceptions, where `try` contains the code that may throw an exception, and `catch` handles it.
What is the `finally` block in Java?::The `finally` block is used to execute code regardless of whether an exception is thrown, often for cleanup tasks.
What is the difference between `throw` and `throws` in Java?::`throw` is used to explicitly throw an exception, while `throws` declares exceptions that a method can throw.
What is multithreading in Java?::Multithreading allows concurrent execution of two or more threads to maximize CPU utilization.
What is the `synchronized` keyword in Java?::The `synchronized` keyword is used to restrict access to a block of code or method to a single thread at a time.
What is the `final` keyword in Java?::The `final` keyword is used to define constants, prevent method overriding, or inheritance of a class.
What is a string in Java?::A string in Java is an immutable sequence of characters represented by the `String` class.
What is the difference between `String`, `StringBuilder`, and `StringBuffer`?::`String` is immutable, `StringBuilder` is mutable and faster, while `StringBuffer` is thread-safe but slower.
What is a collection in Java?::A collection is a framework that provides an architecture to store and manipulate a group of objects, such as lists or sets.
What is an `ArrayList` in Java?::An `ArrayList` is a resizable array implementation in the `java.util` package.
What is a `HashMap` in Java?::A `HashMap` is a collection that stores key-value pairs, allowing efficient retrieval of values based on keys.
What is the difference between `List` and `Set` in Java?::A `List` allows duplicate elements and maintains order, while a `Set` does not allow duplicates and may not maintain order.
What is the `Iterator` interface in Java?::The `Iterator` interface provides methods to traverse elements in a collection.
What is garbage collection in Java?::Garbage collection is an automatic process in Java that deallocates memory for objects no longer in use.

What is the difference between `==` and `.equals()` in Java?::`==` checks reference equality, while `.equals()` checks value equality.
What is the purpose of the `hashCode()` method in Java?::The `hashCode()` method returns an integer value representing the memory address of an object, used in hashing algorithms.

What is the Stream API in Java?::The Stream API, introduced in Java 8, is used to process collections of data in a functional programming style.
What is the `default` keyword in Java interfaces?::The `default` keyword allows methods in interfaces to have a default implementation.
What is a functional interface in Java?::A functional interface has exactly one abstract method and is used with lambda expressions.
What is `try-with-resources` in Java?::`try-with-resources` automatically closes resources, such as files or database connections, after use.
What is the `instanceof` keyword in Java?::The `instanceof` keyword is used to test whether an object is an instance of a specific class or subclass.
What is type casting in Java?::Type casting is the conversion of one data type into another, either explicitly or implicitly.
What is implicit type casting in Java?::Implicit type casting (widening) automatically converts a smaller data type into a larger one, such as `int` to `double`.
What is explicit type casting in Java?::Explicit type casting (narrowing) requires manually converting a larger data type to a smaller one, such as `double` to `int`.
What is the `Math` class in Java?::The `Math` class provides methods for performing mathematical operations like `sqrt()`, `abs()`, and `pow()`.
What is a singleton class in Java?::A singleton class is a design pattern where only one instance of the class can exist.
What is the difference between `abstract` class and `interface` in Java?::An abstract class can have concrete methods, while an interface cannot (prior to Java 8). Interfaces support multiple inheritance, while abstract classes do not.
What is the difference between `throw` and `return` in Java?::`throw` is used to explicitly throw an exception, while `return` ends a method and optionally returns a value.
What is a thread pool in Java?::A thread pool is a collection of pre-initialized threads that can execute tasks, improving performance in multithreaded applications.
What is the difference between `Runnable` and `Thread` in Java?::`Runnable` is an interface that provides a run method, while `Thread` is a class that implements `Runnable` and represents a thread.
What is the `volatile` keyword in Java?::The `volatile` keyword ensures that the value of a variable is always read from main memory, preventing thread caching issues.
What is a race condition in Java?::A race condition occurs when multiple threads access shared resources concurrently, leading to inconsistent results.
What is the `transient` keyword in Java?::The `transient` keyword is used to exclude a variable from being serialized.
What is serialization in Java?::Serialization is the process of converting an object into a byte stream for storage or transmission.

What is an inner class in Java?::An inner class is a class defined within another class, used to logically group classes and enhance encapsulation.
What is a static nested class in Java?::A static nested class is a nested class that does not require an instance of the outer class to be accessed.
What is an anonymous class in Java?::An anonymous class is a class without a name, used for creating one-time implementations of interfaces or abstract classes.
What is the `break` keyword in Java?::The `break` keyword is used to terminate a loop or switch statement prematurely.

What is the `String` pool in Java?::The `String` pool is a special memory region where Java stores string literals to optimize memory usage and improve performance.
What is immutable in Java?::An immutable object cannot be modified after it is created; for example, `String` objects in Java are immutable.
What is a mutable object in Java?::A mutable object can be modified after it is created, such as `StringBuilder` or `ArrayList`.
What is the difference between `Array` and `ArrayList` in Java?::An `Array` has a fixed size, while an `ArrayList` is resizable and part of the `java.util` package.

What is a `Comparator` in Java?::A `Comparator` is an interface used to define custom sorting for objects.

What is the difference between `Comparator` and `Comparable` in Java?::`Comparable` is used for natural ordering, while `Comparator` is used for custom ordering.
What is a `HashSet` in Java?::A `HashSet` is a collection that does not allow duplicate elements and is backed by a `HashMap`.

What is a `TreeMap` in Java?::A `TreeMap` is a map that stores key-value pairs in sorted order based on the keys.
What is a `LinkedHashMap` in Java?::A `LinkedHashMap` is a map that maintains insertion order and provides fast access to elements.
What is an `Iterator` in Java?::An `Iterator` is an object that provides methods to traverse elements of a collection one by one.

What is lazy evaluation in Java Streams?::Lazy evaluation in Java Streams means that intermediate operations on a stream are not executed until a terminal operation is invoked.

What is recursion?::Recursion is a programming technique where a function calls itself to solve smaller instances of a problem.
How can I reverse a string in Python?::You can reverse a string in Python using slicing: `reversed_string = my_string[::-1]`.
What is the purpose of a constructor in OOP?::A constructor initializes an object’s properties when it is created.
How can I merge two dictionaries in Python?::Use the `update()` method or the union operator (`|`) in Python 3.9 and above.
What is the difference between '==' and 'is' in Python?::`==` checks for equality of values, while `is` checks if two objects are the same in memory.
What is a database index?::A database index improves query performance by allowing faster data retrieval.
How does a compiler differ from an interpreter?::A compiler translates the entire code into machine language before execution, while an interpreter translates code line by line.
What is multithreading?::Multithreading allows a program to execute multiple threads simultaneously for better performance.
What is the difference between HTTP and HTTPS?::HTTPS is the secure version of HTTP, using encryption to protect data transfer.
What is a binary search?::Binary search is an algorithm to find an element in a sorted array by repeatedly dividing the search interval in half.
What is cloud computing?::Cloud computing delivers computing resources like storage and applications over the internet.
What is Git?::Git is a distributed version control system used to track changes in code and collaborate on projects.
What is the difference between GET and POST methods in HTTP?::GET requests data from a server, while POST sends data to the server to create or update resources.
What is an API?::An API (Application Programming Interface) allows two applications to communicate with each other.
How can I handle exceptions in Python?::Use `try`, `except`, and optionally `finally` blocks to handle exceptions in Python.
What is a foreign key in databases?::A foreign key is a field in one table that refers to the primary key in another table.
What is a RESTful API?::A RESTful API adheres to REST principles, enabling stateless communication and CRUD operations using standard HTTP methods.
What is JSON?::JSON (JavaScript Object Notation) is a lightweight format for exchanging data between systems.
What is a stack in programming?::A stack is a data structure that follows the Last In, First Out (LIFO) principle.
What is the difference between synchronous and asynchronous programming?::Synchronous code blocks until a task completes, while asynchronous code allows other tasks to run concurrently.
What is Big O notation?::Big O notation describes the efficiency of an algorithm in terms of time and space complexity.
What is inheritance in OOP?::Inheritance allows one class to acquire properties and behaviors from another class.
What is a hash function?::A hash function converts input data into a fixed-size hash value, often used in hashing algorithms and data structures.
What is a virtual machine?::A virtual machine (VM) is an emulation of a physical computer, running an operating system and applications.
What is the difference between primary and secondary memory?::Primary memory (RAM) is fast and volatile, while secondary memory (like HDD/SSD) is slower but persistent.
What is a regular expression?::A regular expression is a pattern used to match character combinations in strings.
What is Docker?::Docker is a platform to build, deploy, and manage containerized applications.
What is continuous integration?::Continuous integration automates the integration of code changes into a shared repository, ensuring regular testing and builds.
What is a microservice?::A microservice is a small, independent service designed to perform a specific task in a larger system.
What is an algorithm?::An algorithm is a step-by-step procedure to solve a problem or perform a computation.
What is a neural network?::A neural network is a machine learning model inspired by the human brain, used for tasks like image recognition and natural language processing.
What is overfitting in machine learning?::Overfitting occurs when a model performs well on training data but poorly on new data.
What is a CDN?::A CDN (Content Delivery Network) accelerates content delivery by caching it at locations closer to users.
What is a load balancer?::A load balancer distributes incoming network traffic across multiple servers to optimize performance and reliability.
What is the Internet of Things (IoT)?::IoT refers to devices connected to the internet, enabling them to collect and exchange data.
What is blockchain?::Blockchain is a decentralized ledger technology that records transactions securely and transparently.
What is virtual memory?::Virtual memory is a system that uses a portion of secondary storage as if it were primary memory to extend available memory.
What is caching?::Caching stores frequently accessed data temporarily to improve performance and reduce load on a system.
What is an IP address?::An IP address is a unique identifier for a device on a network.
What is a session in web development?::A session stores user-specific data during their interaction with a web application.
What is a cookie in web development?::A cookie is a small piece of data stored on a user's browser by a website to remember preferences or track activity.
What is recursion?::Recursion is a programming technique where a function calls itself to solve smaller instances of a problem.
What is NAT?::Network Address Translation (NAT) modifies network address information in IP packet headers for routing purposes.
What is a proxy server?::A proxy server acts as an intermediary between a client and the internet, enhancing security and privacy.
What is an object in OOP?::An object is an instance of a class that encapsulates data and methods.
What is polymorphism in OOP?::Polymorphism allows objects to be treated as instances of their parent class, enabling flexibility and reuse.
What is a deadlock?::A deadlock occurs when two or more processes are unable to proceed because each is waiting for the other to release resources.
What is the difference between SQL and NoSQL databases?::SQL databases are structured and relational, while NoSQL databases are flexible and non-relational, suitable for unstructured data.
What is a cache miss?::A cache miss occurs when the requested data is not found in the cache and must be fetched from the main memory or source.
What is a firewall?::A firewall is a security system that monitors and controls incoming and outgoing network traffic based on predefined rules.
What is Kubernetes?::Kubernetes is an open-source platform for automating deployment, scaling, and management of containerized applications.
What is a thread in programming?::A thread is the smallest unit of a program that can be executed independently.
What is a race condition?::A race condition occurs when multiple threads or processes access shared resources concurrently, leading to unpredictable behavior.
What is a semaphore?::A semaphore is a synchronization primitive used to control access to a common resource by multiple threads.
What is a binary tree?::A binary tree is a hierarchical data structure where each node has at most two child nodes.
What is a linked list?::A linked list is a data structure consisting of nodes, each containing data and a reference to the next node.
What is the OSI model?::The OSI model is a conceptual framework that standardizes networking functions into seven layers.
What is a router?::A router is a device that forwards data packets between computer networks.
What is a switch?::A switch is a networking device that connects devices within a network and uses MAC addresses to forward data to the correct destination.
What is ARP?::The Address Resolution Protocol (ARP) maps IP addresses to MAC addresses within a local network.
What is a subnet mask?::A subnet mask divides an IP address into network and host portions, enabling efficient IP address allocation.
What is a VPN?::A Virtual Private Network (VPN) creates a secure, encrypted connection over the internet to protect data and privacy.
What is a kernel?::The kernel is the core of an operating system, managing hardware resources and system processes.
What is a process in computing?::A process is an instance of a program in execution, including its code, data, and state.
What is a thread pool?::A thread pool is a collection of pre-initialized threads that execute tasks to improve efficiency in multithreaded applications.
What is a mutex?::A mutex is a synchronization primitive that ensures only one thread can access a resource at a time.
What is paging?::Paging is a memory management scheme that eliminates the need for contiguous memory allocation by dividing memory into fixed-size pages.
What is fragmentation in memory management?::Fragmentation occurs when memory is used inefficiently, leaving unusable gaps.
What is a database transaction?::A transaction is a sequence of operations performed as a single logical unit of work, ensuring data consistency.
What is ACID in databases?::ACID stands for Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation, and Durability, ensuring reliable database transactions.
What is normalization?::Normalization organizes database tables to reduce redundancy and improve data integrity.
What is denormalization?::Denormalization introduces redundancy into a database to improve query performance at the cost of storage efficiency.
What is a JOIN in SQL?::A JOIN combines rows from two or more tables based on a related column.
What is a stored procedure?::A stored procedure is a precompiled set of SQL statements that can be executed as a single function.

How does a compiler differ from an interpreter?::A compiler translates the entire code into machine language before execution, while an interpreter translates code line by line.
What is multithreading?::Multithreading allows a program to execute multiple threads simultaneously for better performance.
What is the difference between HTTP and HTTPS?::HTTPS is the secure version of HTTP, using encryption to protect data transfer.
What is a binary search?::Binary search is an algorithm to find an element in a sorted array by repeatedly dividing the search interval in half.
What is cloud computing?::Cloud computing delivers computing resources like storage and applications over the internet.
What is Git?::Git is a distributed version control system used to track changes in code and collaborate on projects.
What is the difference between GET and POST methods in HTTP?::GET requests data from a server, while POST sends data to the server to create or update resources.
What is an API?::An API (Application Programming Interface) allows two applications to communicate with each other.
How can I handle exceptions in Python?::Use `try`, `except`, and optionally `finally` blocks to handle exceptions in Python.
What is a foreign key in databases?::A foreign key is a field in one table that refers to the primary key in another table.
What is a RESTful API?::A RESTful API adheres to REST principles, enabling stateless communication and CRUD operations using standard HTTP methods.
What is JSON?::JSON (JavaScript Object Notation) is a lightweight format for exchanging data between systems.
What is a stack in programming?::A stack is a data structure that follows the Last In, First Out (LIFO) principle.
What is the difference between synchronous and asynchronous programming?::Synchronous code blocks until a task completes, while asynchronous code allows other tasks to run concurrently.
What is Big O notation?::Big O notation describes the efficiency of an algorithm in terms of time and space complexity.
What is inheritance in OOP?::Inheritance allows one class to acquire properties and behaviors from another class.
What is a hash function?::A hash function converts input data into a fixed-size hash value, often used in hashing algorithms and data structures.
What is a virtual machine?::A virtual machine (VM) is an emulation of a physical computer, running an operating system and applications.
What is the difference between primary and secondary memory?::Primary memory (RAM) is fast and volatile, while secondary memory (like HDD/SSD) is slower but persistent.
What is a regular expression?::A regular expression is a pattern used to match character combinations in strings.
What is Docker?::Docker is a platform to build, deploy, and manage containerized applications.
What is continuous integration?::Continuous integration automates the integration of code changes into a shared repository, ensuring regular testing and builds.
What is a microservice?::A microservice is a small, independent service designed to perform a specific task in a larger system.
What is an algorithm?::An algorithm is a step-by-step procedure to solve a problem or perform a computation.
What is a neural network?::A neural network is a machine learning model inspired by the human brain, used for tasks like image recognition and natural language processing.
What is overfitting in machine learning?::Overfitting occurs when a model performs well on training data but poorly on new data.
What is a CDN?::A CDN (Content Delivery Network) accelerates content delivery by caching it at locations closer to users.
What is a load balancer?::A load balancer distributes incoming network traffic across multiple servers to optimize performance and reliability.
What is the Internet of Things (IoT)?::IoT refers to devices connected to the internet, enabling them to collect and exchange data.
What is blockchain?::Blockchain is a decentralized ledger technology that records transactions securely and transparently.
What is virtual memory?::Virtual memory is a system that uses a portion of secondary storage as if it were primary memory to extend available memory.
What is caching?::Caching stores frequently accessed data temporarily to improve performance and reduce load on a system.
What is an IP address?::An IP address is a unique identifier for a device on a network.
What is a session in web development?::A session stores user-specific data during their interaction with a web application.
What is a cookie in web development?::A cookie is a small piece of data stored on a user's browser by a website to remember preferences or track activity.
What is recursion?::Recursion is a programming technique where a function calls itself to solve smaller instances of a problem.
What is NAT?::Network Address Translation (NAT) modifies network address information in IP packet headers for routing purposes.
What is a proxy server?::A proxy server acts as an intermediary between a client and the internet, enhancing security and privacy.
What is an object in OOP?::An object is an instance of a class that encapsulates data and methods.
What is polymorphism in OOP?::Polymorphism allows objects to be treated as instances of their parent class, enabling flexibility and reuse.
What is a deadlock?::A deadlock occurs when two or more processes are unable to proceed because each is waiting for the other to release resources.
What is the difference between SQL and NoSQL databases?::SQL databases are structured and relational, while NoSQL databases are flexible and non-relational, suitable for unstructured data.
What is a cache miss?::A cache miss occurs when the requested data is not found in the cache and must be fetched from the main memory or source.
What is a firewall?::A firewall is a security system that monitors and controls incoming and outgoing network traffic based on predefined rules.
What is Kubernetes?::Kubernetes is an open-source platform for automating deployment, scaling, and management of containerized applications.
What is a thread in programming?::A thread is the smallest unit of a program that can be executed independently.
What is a race condition?::A race condition occurs when multiple threads or processes access shared resources concurrently, leading to unpredictable behavior.
What is a semaphore?::A semaphore is a synchronization primitive used to control access to a common resource by multiple threads.
What is a binary tree?::A binary tree is a hierarchical data structure where each node has at most two child nodes.
What is a linked list?::A linked list is a data structure consisting of nodes, each containing data and a reference to the next node.
What is the OSI model?::The OSI model is a conceptual framework that standardizes networking functions into seven layers.
What is a router?::A router is a device that forwards data packets between computer networks.
What is a switch?::A switch is a networking device that connects devices within a network and uses MAC addresses to forward data to the correct destination.
What is ARP?::The Address Resolution Protocol (ARP) maps IP addresses to MAC addresses within a local network.
What is a subnet mask?::A subnet mask divides an IP address into network and host portions, enabling efficient IP address allocation.
What is a VPN?::A Virtual Private Network (VPN) creates a secure, encrypted connection over the internet to protect data and privacy.
What is a kernel?::The kernel is the core of an operating system, managing hardware resources and system processes.
What is a process in computing?::A process is an instance of a program in execution, including its code, data, and state.
What is a thread pool?::A thread pool is a collection of pre-initialized threads that execute tasks to improve efficiency in multithreaded applications.
What is a mutex?::A mutex is a synchronization primitive that ensures only one thread can access a resource at a time.
What is paging?::Paging is a memory management scheme that eliminates the need for contiguous memory allocation by dividing memory into fixed-size pages.
What is fragmentation in memory management?::Fragmentation occurs when memory is used inefficiently, leaving unusable gaps.
What is a database transaction?::A transaction is a sequence of operations performed as a single logical unit of work, ensuring data consistency.
What is ACID in databases?::ACID stands for Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation, and Durability, ensuring reliable database transactions.
What is normalization?::Normalization organizes database tables to reduce redundancy and improve data integrity.
What is denormalization?::Denormalization introduces redundancy into a database to improve query performance at the cost of storage efficiency.
What is a JOIN in SQL?::A JOIN combines rows from two or more tables based on a related column.
What is a stored procedure?::A stored procedure is a precompiled set of SQL statements that can be executed as a single function.
What is recursion?::Recursion is a programming technique where a function calls itself to solve smaller instances of a problem.
How can I reverse a string in Python?::You can reverse a string in Python using slicing: `reversed_string = my_string[::-1]`.
What is the purpose of a constructor in OOP?::A constructor initializes an object’s properties when it is created.
How can I merge two dictionaries in Python?::Use the `update()` method or the union operator (`|`) in Python 3.9 and above.
What is the difference between '==' and 'is' in Python?::`==` checks for equality of values, while `is` checks if two objects are the same in memory.
